{{Multiple image
| footer = [[Angelique Kerber]] won her first Grand Slam title at the [[2016 Australian Open|Australian Open]], thus becoming the first German to win a Grand Slam title since [[Steffi Graf]] at the [[1999 French Open]] defeating [[List of WTA number 1 ranked tennis players|World No. 1]] [[Serena Williams]] in the final. Kerber would go on to win the [[2016 US Open (tennis)|2016 US Open]], defeating [[Karolína Plíšková]] in the final, thus would attain her World No. 1 ranking. [[Garbiñe Muguruza]] won her first Grand Slam title at the [[2016 French Open|French Open]], thus becoming the first Spaniard to win a Grand Slam title since [[Arantxa Sánchez Vicario]] at the [[1998 French Open]] by defeating Williams in the final. Williams herself would go on to reach the season's third Grand Slam finals and defeat Kerber in the final at [[2016 Wimbledon Championships|Wimbledon]] to claim her 22nd Grand Slam title, equaling [[Steffi Graf]]'s record for most Grand Slam titles in the [[Open Era]].

| image1    = Angelique Kerber (18954256629).jpg

The '''2016 WTA Tour''' was the elite professional [[tennis]] circuit organised by the [[Women's Tennis Association]] (WTA) for the 2016 tennis season. The 2016 WTA Tour calendar comprises the [[Grand Slam (tennis)|Grand Slam]] tournaments (supervised by the [[International Tennis Federation]] (ITF), the [[WTA Premier tournaments]] (Premier Mandatory, Premier 5, and regular Premier), the [[WTA International tournaments]], the [[Fed Cup]] (organized by the ITF), the year-end championships (the [[WTA Tour Championships]] and the [[WTA Elite Trophy]]). Also included in the 2016 calendar is the [[Tennis at the 2016 Summer Olympics|Summer Olympic Games]] and [[Hopman Cup]], which were organized by the ITF and did not distribute ranking points.<ref name=WTACalendar2016>{{cite web|work=wtatennis.com|publisher=WTA Tour, Inc.|title=2016 WTA calendar|url=http://www.wtatennis.com/SEWTATour-Archive/Archive/AboutTheTour/TourCalendar_2016.pdf|accessdate=2015-06-11|format=PDF}}</ref>

==Statistical information==
These tables present the number of [[Types of tennis match#Singles|singles]] (S), [[Types of tennis match#Doubles|doubles]] (D), and [[Mixed doubles tennis|mixed doubles]] (X) titles won by each player and each nation during the season, within all the tournament categories of the 2016 WTA Tour: the [[Grand Slam (tennis)|Grand Slam]] tournaments, the [[Tennis at the 2016 Summer Olympics|tennis event]] at the [[2016 Summer Olympics|Rio de Janeiro Summer Olympic Games]], the year-end championships (the [[WTA Tour Championships]] and the [[Commonwealth Bank Tournament of Champions|Tournament of Champions]]), the [[WTA Premier tournaments]] (Premier Mandatory, Premier 5, and regular Premier), and the [[WTA International tournaments]].<ref name=WTACalendar2016/> The players/nations are sorted by: 1) total number of titles (a doubles title won by two players representing the same nation counts as only one win for the nation); 2) cumulated importance of those titles (one Grand Slam win equalling two Premier Mandatory/Premier 5 wins, one year-end championships win equalling one-and-a-half Premier Mandatory/Premier 5 win, one Premier Mandatory/Premier 5 win equalling two Premier wins, one Olympic win equalling one-and-a-half Premier win, one Premier win equalling two International wins); 3) a singles > doubles > mixed doubles hierarchy; 4) alphabetical order (by family names for players).

== Prize money leaders ==
Angelique Kerber topped the 2016 money list and joined Serena Williams as the only two women to ever win over $10,000,000 in a single season. Additionally, Kerber became the 15th WTA player to win $20,000,000 in career earnings. The top-32 players earned over $1,000,000.  Bethanie Mattek-Sands won $1,088,600 in doubles tournaments.  It was the 3rd consecutive year that a player earned over $1,000,000 in doubles events.

== Retirements ==
Following is a list of notable players (winners of a main tour title, and/or part of the [[WTA Rankings]] top 100 (singles) or (doubles) for at least one week) who announced their retirement from professional tennis, became inactive (after not playing for more than 52 weeks), or were permanently banned from playing, during the 2016 season:

*{{flagicon|SWE}} '''[[Sofia Arvidsson]]''' ''(born 16 February 1984, in [[Halmstad]], Sweden)'' – She decided to retire in January 2016 at the age of 31.<ref>{{cite web | url=http://www.wtatennis.com/news/article/5257735/title/arvidsson-dreams-of-life-post-tennis | title=Arvidsson Dreams Of Life Post-Tennis | accessdate=9 January 2016}}</ref>
*{{flagicon|CZE}} '''[[Gabriela Chmelinová]]''' ''(born 2 June 1976 in [[Prague]], Czechoslovakia)'' – Chmelinová announced her retirement from professional tennis in 2016.
*{{flagicon|ESP}} '''[[Lourdes Domínguez Lino]]''' ''(born 31 March 1981 in [[Pontevedra]], Spain)'' – She decided to retire in November 2016 at the age of 35.<ref>{{cite web | url=http://www.tennisworldusa.org/news/news/WTA_Tennis/37851/former-top-40-player-lourdes-dominguez-lino-retires-from-tennis/ | title=Former Top 40 Player Lourdes Dominguez Lino Retires From Tennis | accessdate=1 November 2016}}</ref>
*{{flagicon|CAN}} '''[[Maureen Drake]]''' ''(born 21 March 1971 in [[Toronto]], Canada)'' – She announced her second and permanent retirement from professional tennis in August 2016.
*{{flagicon|SVK}} '''[[Janette Husárová]]''' ''(born 4 June 1974 in [[Bratislava]], Slovakia)'' – In February 2016 Husárová announced her retirement from professional tennis.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.livetennis.it/post/232094/si-ritira-janette-husarova/|title=Si ritira Janette Husarova|website=livetennis.it|accessdate=18 March 2018}}</ref>
*'''{{flagicon|SRB}} [[Ana Ivanovic]]''' ''(born 6 November 1987 in [[Belgrade]], Serbia)'' – '''The former world number 1''' announced her retirement from professional tennis December 2016.
*{{flagicon|POL}} '''[[Klaudia Jans-Ignacik]]''' ''(born 24 September 1984 in [[Gdynia]], Poland)'' – She announced her retirement from professional tennis in August 2016.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.facebook.com/Klaudia.J.I/photos/a.403342443062681.95993.402964456433813/1176670049063246/?type=1&theater|title=Klaudia Jans Ignacik Official|website=www.facebook.com|accessdate=18 March 2018}}</ref>
*{{flagicon|FRA}} '''[[Mathilde Johansson]]''' ''(born 28 April 1985, in [[Boulogne-Billancourt]], France)'' – Johansson played her final match in the singles [[2016 French Open]] qualifications.<ref>{{cite web | url=https://twitter.com/rolandgarros_FR/status/732891822477987840 | title=.@JohanssonMath l'a confirmé après sa victoire au 1er tour des qualifications : ce sera son dernier tournoi. #RG16 | accessdate=19 May 2016}}</ref>
*{{flagicon|AUT}} '''[[Sandra Klemenschits]]''' ''(born 13 November 1982 in [[Salzburg]], Austria)'' – She announced her retirement from professional tennis in October 2016.
*{{flagicon|RUS}} '''[[Maria Kondratieva]]''' ''(born 17 January 1982 in [[Moscow]], Russia)'' – Kondratieva announced her retirement from professional tennis in 2016.
*{{flagicon|CZE}} '''[[Klára Koukalová]]''' ''(born 24 February 1982 in [[Prague]], Czech Republic)'' – She announced her retirement from professional tennis in September 2016.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://sportowefakty.wp.pl/tenis/633066/klara-koukalova-zakonczyla-kariere|title=Klara Koukalova zakończyła karierę - WP SportoweFakty|first=Wirtualna Polska|last=Media|date=26 September 2016|website=wp.pl|accessdate=18 March 2018|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20161014030038/http://sportowefakty.wp.pl/tenis/633066/klara-koukalova-zakonczyla-kariere|archive-date=14 October 2016|url-status=dead}}</ref>
*{{flagicon|SLO}} '''[[Petra Rampre]]''' ''(born 20 January 1980 in [[Ljubljana]], Slovenia)'' – Rampre announced her retirement from professional tennis in 2016.
*{{flagicon|THA}} '''[[Tamarine Tanasugarn]]''' ''(born 24 May 1977, in [[Los Angeles]], United States)'' – She announced her retirement from professional tennis in June 2016.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.nationmultimedia.com/breakingnews/Tammy-says-goodbye-to-professional-tennis-30288653.html|title=Tammy says goodbye to professional tennis  - The Nation|website=nationmultimedia.com|accessdate=18 March 2018}}</ref>
*{{flagicon|CZE}} '''[[Vladimíra Uhlířová]]''' ''(born 4 May 1978 in [[České Budějovice]], Czechoslovakia)'' – She announced her retirement from professional tennis in January 2016.
*{{flagicon|CZE}} '''[[Nicole Vaidišová]]''' ''(born 23 April 1989 in [[Nuremberg]], West Germany)'' – She announced her second and permanent retirement from professional tennis in July 2016.<ref>{{cite web | url=https://www.instagram.com/p/BIFD2y-AP7F/|title=Nicki Vaidisova on Instagram: "So...This has been one of the hardest words for me to write.After months and months of thinking and agonizing about this, I have decided to…" | accessdate=20 July 2016}}</ref>
*{{flagicon|LIE}} '''[[Stephanie Vogt]]''' ''(born 15 February 1990 in [[Vaduz]], Liechtenstein)'' – She announced her retirement from professional tennis in August 2016.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.vaterland.li/liechtenstein/sport/Stephanie-Vogt-beendet-ihre-Karriere;art174,217482|title=Stephanie Vogt beendet ihre Karriere|website=vaterland.li|accessdate=18 March 2018}}</ref>
*{{flagicon|HKG}} '''[[Yan Zi (tennis)|Yan Zi]]''' ''(born 12 November 1984 in [[Sichuan]], China)'' – Yan Zi announced her retirement from professional tennis in 2016.
